Isn't the R3 going to run into problems with regulators in the USA? The rear light bar fully goes up when you lift the trunk. I've heard that's not allowed in the USA, the brake lights must not be attached to the trunk. Quick Google search: "A federal regulation states that brake lights must be on a part of the vehicle that doesn't move. This means that while a trunk can have redundant lights, some of the lights must be on the bumper or side"

Rivian was very strategic in their release cycle. By releasing an $80,000 version of their car first, the R1S, it put in the public‚Äôs mind that this is a premium product. Now we are going to release a better version of it for $45,000. So everyone wants to get their hands on it. Whereas if they had released a $45k car first, then the brand perception is like it‚Äôs a KIA or Chevy EV. I don‚Äôt need to run to get my hands on it. So even though they have been running very lean and not making any profit, it‚Äôs all on purpose. They only built and shipped 44,000 R1S‚Äô on purpose. It‚Äôs just a premium car to establish the brand, get the public aware of it on the road. You see one in the wild and you get excited and curious. You realize it's a crazy purchase and not totally attainable. Then you find out they're making a version that's half the price. The next car is going to be at scale and they are going to make tons of them all over the world. I'm not sure their naming convention is going to make a whole lot of sense to people. Their first products R1T & R1S made sense. They were the first vehicles produced so you had R1 and then the T for truck and S for SUV. Now you have an R2 which is smaller than the R1S, but still an SUV, but the name doesn't have the S in it. You also have the R3 which is more of a cross-over style vehicle and smaller than both the R1 and R2. so as the numbers get bigger, the vehicle gets smaller (counter-intuitive) and the new vehicles don't use the letters. I do feel like the naming scheme is a lost opportunity however, I think they should have taken a page out of Subaru's book along the lines of what they did with the Outback name in the past. Why did Rivian choose to put the NACS port on the passenger side rear? If you want to make it work with Tesla Superchargers, Driver rear or Passenger front are the ideal locations to help reduce wasting Supercharger resources and taking up 2 charger spots for just one vehicle, at Tesla V3 chargers. V4 has a longer cable and works for both sides, so not as big of a deal, but front passenger port would have been nice to help when towing and supercharger compatibility.
